<a id="1450" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="1455" class="Keyword">import</a> <a id="1462" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.html" class="Module">Relation.Nullary</a> <a id="1479" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="1485" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="1486" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.html#534" class="Datatype">Dec</a><a id="1489" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="1491" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.html#570" class="InductiveConstructor">yes</a><a id="1494" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="1496" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.html#597" class="InductiveConstructor">no</a><a id="1498" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="1500" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="1505" class="Keyword">import</a> <a id="1512" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Function.html" class="Module">Function</a> <a id="1521" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="1527" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="1528" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Function.html#769" class="Function Operator">_âˆ˜_</a><a id="1531" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Having proved a preservation property in the last chapter, a natural
next step would be to prove progress. That is, to prove a property
of the form

    If Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v, then either M is a lambda abstraction or M â€”â†’ N for some N.

Such a property would tell us that having a denotation implies either
reduction to normal form or divergence. This is indeed true, but we
can prove a much stronger property! In fact, having a denotation that
is a function value (not `âŠ¥`) implies reduction to a lambda
abstraction (no divergence).

This stronger property, reformulated a bit, is known as _adequacy_.
That is, if a term `M` is denotationally equal to a lambda abstraction,
then `M` reduces to a lambda abstraction.

    â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)  implies M â€”â†  Æ› N' for some N'

Recall that `â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)` is equivalent to saying that
`Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` for some `v` and `w`. We will show that
`Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` implies reduction a lambda abstraction.

It is well known that a term can reduce to a lambda abstraction using
full Î² reduction if and only if it can reduce to a lambda abstraction
using the call-by-name reduction strategy. So we shall prove that
`Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` implies that `M` halts under call-by-name evaluation,
which we define with a big-step semantics written `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ c`, where
`c` is a closure (a term paired with an environment) and `Î³'` is an
environment that maps variables to closures

So we will show that `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (v â†¦ w)` implies `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ c`,
provided `Î³` and `Î³'` are appropriate related.  The proof will
be an induction on the derivation of `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, and to
strengthen the induction hypothesis, we will relate semantic values to
closures using a _logical relation_ `ğ•`.

The rest of this chapter is organized as follows.

* We loosen the requirement that `M` result in a function value and
  instead require that `M` result in a value that is greater than or
  equal to a function value. We establish several properties about
  being ``greater than a function''.

* We define the call-by-name big-step semantics of the lambda calculus
  and prove that it is deterministic.

* We define the logical relation `ğ•` that relates values and closures,
  and extend it to a relation on terms `ğ”¼` and environments `ğ”¾`.

* We prove the main lemma,
  that if `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'` and `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, then `ğ”¼ v (clos M Î³')`.

* We prove adequacy as a corollary to the main lemma.


## The property of being greater or equal to a function

We define the following short-hand for saying that a value is
greather-than or equal to a function value.

If a value `u` is greater than a function, then an even greater value `u'`
is too.

If the join of two values `u` and `u'` is greater than a function, then
at least one of them is too.

On the other hand, if neither of `u` and `u'` is greater than a function,
then their join is also not greater than a function.

The converse is also true. If the join of two values is not above a
function, then neither of them is individually.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="not-AboveFun-âŠ”-inv"></a><a id="5751" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#5751" class="Function">not-AboveFun-âŠ”-inv</a> <a id="5770" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5772" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="5774" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#5774" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="5776" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#5776" class="Bound">u&#39;</a> <a id="5779" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5781" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#3989" class="Datatype">Value</a><a id="5786" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="5788" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="5790" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.html#464" class="Function Operator">Â¬</a> <a id="5792" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4094" class="Function">AboveFun</a> <a id="5801" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5802" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#5774" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="5804" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#4051" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŠ”</a> <a id="5806" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#5776" class="Bound">u&#39;</a><a id="5808" class="Symbol">)</a>
              <a id="5824" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="5826" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.html#464" class="Function Operator">Â¬</a> <a id="5828" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4094" class="Function">AboveFun</a> <a id="5837" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#5774" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="5839" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Data.Product.html#1353" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a> <a id="5841" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.html#464" class="Function Operator">Â¬</a> <a id="5843" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4094" class="Function">AboveFun</a> <a id="5852" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#5776" class="Bound">u&#39;</a>

The property of being greater than a function value is decidable, as
exhibited by the following function.

## Relating values to closures

Next we relate semantic values to closures.  The relation `ğ•` is for
closures whose term is a lambda abstraction, i.e., in weak-head normal
form (WHNF). The relation ğ”¼ is for any closure. Roughly speaking,
`ğ”¼ v c` will hold if, when `v` is greater than a function value, `c` evaluates
to a closure `c'` in WHNF and `ğ• v c'`. Regarding `ğ• v c`, it will hold when
`c` is in WHNF, and if `v` is a function, the body of `c` evaluates
according to `v`.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="ğ•"></a><a id="7205" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7205" class="Function">ğ•</a> <a id="7207" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="7209" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#3989" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="7215" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7217" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2458" class="Datatype">Clos</a> <a id="7222" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7224" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>
<a id="ğ”¼"></a><a id="7228" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7228" class="Function">ğ”¼</a> <a id="7230" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="7232" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#3989" class="Datatype">Value</a> <a id="7238" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7240" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2458" class="Datatype">Clos</a> <a id="7245" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="7247" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

We define `ğ•` as a function from values and closures to `Set` and not as a
data type because it is mutually recursive with `ğ”¼` in a negative
position (to the left of an implication).  We first perform case
analysis on the term in the closure. If the term is a variable or
application, then `ğ•` is false (`Bot`). If the term is a lambda
abstraction, we define `ğ•` by recursion on the value, which we
describe below.

class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="7954" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

* If the value is `âŠ¥`, then the result is true (`âŠ¤`).

* If the value is a join (u âŠ” v), then the result is the pair
  (conjunction) of ğ• is true for both u and v.

* The important case is for a function value `v â†¦ w` and closure
  `clos (Æ› N) Î³`. Given any closure `c` such that `ğ”¼ v c`, if `w` is
  greater than a function, then `N` evaluates (with `Î³` extended with `c`)
  to some closure `c'` and we have `ğ• w c'`.


The definition of `ğ”¼` is straightforward. If `v` is a greater than a
function, then `M` evaluates to a closure related to `v`.

%}{% raw %}#3020" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="8580" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8540" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="8582" href="{% endraw class="Bound">c</a> <a id="8586" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Data.Product.html#1353" class="Function Operator">Ã—</a> <a id="8588" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7205" class="Function">ğ•</a> <a id="8590" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8532" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="8592" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8564" class="Bound">c</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

The proof of the main lemma is by induction on `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, so it goes
underneath lambda abstractions and must therefore reason about open
terms (terms with variables). So we must relate environments of
semantic values to environments of closures.  In the following, `ğ”¾`
relates `Î³` to `Î³'` if the corresponding values and closures are related
by `ğ”¼`.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="ğ”¾"></a><a id="8972" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8972" class="Function">ğ”¾</a> <a id="8974" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8976" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="8978" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8978" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="8979" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="8981" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8983" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Denotational.md %}{% raw %}#7223" class="Function">Env</a> <a id="8987" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8978" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="8989" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="8991" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2428" class="Function">ClosEnv</a> <a id="8999" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#8978" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9001" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9003" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a>

We need a few properties of the `ğ•` and `ğ”¼` relations.  The first is that
a closure in the `ğ•` relation must be in weak-head normal form.  We
define WHNF has follows.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="9424" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="WHNF"></a><a id="9429" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9429" class="Datatype">WHNF</a> <a id="9434" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9436" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="9438" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9439" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9439" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9441" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9441" class="Bound">A</a><a id="9442" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9444" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9446" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9439" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9448" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4150" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="9450" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9441" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9452" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9454" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9458" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="WHNF.Æ›_"></a><a id="9466" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9466" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›_</a> <a id="9469" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9471" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="9473" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9474" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9474" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="9475" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9477" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9478" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9478" class="Bound">N</a> <a id="9480" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9482" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9474" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9484" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3018" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="9486" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2694" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a> <a id="9488" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4150" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="9490" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2694" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="9491" class="Symbol">}</a>
     <a id="9498" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9500" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9429" class="Datatype">WHNF</a> <a id="9505" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9506" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4238" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›</a> <a id="9508" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9478" class="Bound">N</a><a id="9509" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

The proof goes by cases on the term in the closure.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="ğ•â†’WHNF"></a><a id="9589" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9589" class="Function">ğ•â†’WHNF</a> <a id="9596" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9598" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="9600" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9600" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="9601" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9603" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9603" class="Bound">Î³</a> <a id="9605" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9607" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2428" class="Function">ClosEnv</a> <a id="9615" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9600" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="9616" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9618" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9618" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="9620" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9622" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9600" class="Bound">Î“</a> <a id="9624" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4150" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="9626" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2694" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="9627" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9629" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9629" class="Bound">v</a><a id="9630" class="Symbol">}</a>
       <a id="9639" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9641" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#7205" class="Function">ğ•</a> <a id="9643" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9629" class="Bound">v</a> <a id="9645" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9646" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2477" class="InductiveConstructor">clos</a> <a id="9651" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9618" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="9653" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9603" class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="9654" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="9656" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="9658" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9429" class="Datatype">WHNF</a> <a id="9663" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9618" class="Bound">M</a>

Next we have an introduction rule for `ğ•` that mimics the `âŠ”-intro`
rule. If both `u` and `v` are related to a closure `c`, then their join is
too.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="ğ•âŠ”-intro"></a><a id="9918" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9918" class="Function">ğ•âŠ”-intro</a> <a id="9927" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9929" class="Symbol">âˆ€{</a><a id="9931" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9931" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="9933" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9933" class="Bound">u</a> <a id="9935" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#9935" class="Bound">v</a><a id="9936" class="Symbol">}</a>

In a moment we prove that `ğ•` is preserved when going from a greater
value to a lesser value: if `ğ• v c` and `v' âŠ‘ v`, then `ğ• v' c`.
This property, named `ğ•-sub`, is needed by the main lemma in
the case for the `sub` rule.

To prove `ğ•-sub`, we in turn need the following property concerning
values that are not greater than a function, that is, values that are
equivalent to `âŠ¥`. In such cases, `ğ• v (clos (Æ› N) Î³')` is trivially true.

The proofs of `ğ•-sub` and `ğ”¼-sub` are intertwined.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="sub-ğ•"></a><a id="11026" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#11026" class="Function">sub-ğ•</a> <a id="11032" <a id="sub-ğ”¼"></a><a id="11078" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#11078" class="Function">sub-ğ”¼</a> <a id="11084" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11086" We prove `ğ•-sub` by case analysis on the closure's term, to dispatch the
cases for variables and application. We then proceed by induction on
`v' âŠ‘ v`. We describe each case below.

<a id="12921" class="Symbol">...</a> <a id="12925" class="Symbol">|</a> <a id="12927" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Data.Sum.Base.html#475" class="InductiveConstructor">injâ‚</a> <a id="12932" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12932" class="Bound">af2</a> <a id="12936" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12938" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Data.Empty.html#360" class="Function">âŠ¥-elim</a> <a id="12945" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12946" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.Negation.html#560" class="Function">contradiction</a> <a id="12960" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12932" class="Bound">af2</a> <a id="12964" class="Bound">naf2</a><a id="12968" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="12970" class="Symbol">...</a> <a id="12974" class="Symbol">|</a> <a id="12976" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Data.Sum.Base.html#500" class="InductiveConstructor">injâ‚‚</a> <a id="12981" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12981" class="Bound">af3</a> <a id="12985" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12987" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Data.Empty.html#360" class="Function">âŠ¥-elim</a> <a id="12994" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12995" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Relation.Nullary.Negation.html#560" class="Function">contradiction</a> <a id="13009" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#12981" class="Bound">af3</a> <a id="13013" class="Bound">naf3</a><a id="13017" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

* Case `BotâŠ‘`. We immediately have `ğ• âŠ¥ (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `ConjLâŠ‘`.

        vâ‚' âŠ‘ v     vâ‚‚' âŠ‘ v
        -------------------
        (vâ‚' âŠ” vâ‚‚') âŠ‘ v

  The induction hypotheses gives us `ğ• vâ‚' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`
  and `ğ• vâ‚‚' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`, which is all we need for this case. 

* Case `ConjR1âŠ‘`.

        v' âŠ‘ vâ‚
        -------------
        v' âŠ‘ (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)

  The induction hypothesis gives us `ğ• v' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `ConjR2âŠ‘`.

        v' âŠ‘ vâ‚‚
        -------------
        v' âŠ‘ (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)

  Again, the induction hypothesis gives us `ğ• v' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `TransâŠ‘`.

        v' âŠ‘ vâ‚‚   vâ‚‚ âŠ‘ v
        -----------------
             v' âŠ‘ v

  The induction hypothesis for `vâ‚‚ âŠ‘ v` gives us
  `ğ• vâ‚‚ (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`. We apply the induction hypothesis
  for `v' âŠ‘ vâ‚‚` to conclude that `ğ• v' (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`.

* Case `DistâŠ‘`. This case  is the most difficult. We have

        ğ• (v â†¦ w) (clos (Æ› N) Î³)
        ğ• (v â†¦ w') (clos (Æ› N) Î³)

  and need to show that 

        ğ• (v â†¦ (w âŠ” w')) (clos (Æ› N) Î³)
  
  Let `c` be an arbtrary closure such that `ğ”¼ v c`.
  Assume `w âŠ” w'` is greater than a function.
  Unfortunately, this does not mean that both `w` and `w'`
  are above functions. But thanks to the lemma `AboveFun-âŠ”`,
  we know that at least one of them is greater than a function.
  
  * Suppose both of them are greater than a function.  Then we have
    `Î³ âŠ¢ N â‡“ clos L Î´` and `ğ• w (clos L Î´)`.  We also have `Î³ âŠ¢ N â‡“ câ‚ƒ` and
    `ğ• w' câ‚ƒ`.  Because the big-step semantics is deterministic, we have
    `câ‚ƒ â‰¡ clos L Î´`. Also, from `ğ• w (clos L Î´)` we know that `L â‰¡ Æ› N'`
    for some `N'`. We conclude that `ğ• (w âŠ” w') (clos (Æ› N') Î´)`.

  * Suppose one of them is greater than a function and the other is
    not: say `AboveFun w` and `Â¬ AboveFun w'`. Then from
    `ğ• (v â†¦ w) (clos (Æ› N) Î³)`
    we have `Î³ âŠ¢ N â‡“ clos L Î³â‚` and `ğ• w (clos L Î³â‚)`. From this we have
    `L â‰¡ Æ› N'` for some `N'`. Meanwhile, from `Â¬ AboveFun w'` we have
    `ğ• w' (clos L Î³â‚)`. We conclude that
    `ğ• (w âŠ” w') (clos (Æ› N') Î³â‚)`.
    

The proof of `sub-ğ”¼` is direct and explained below.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="15144" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#11078" class="Function">sub-ğ”¼</a> <a id="15150" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="15151" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2477" class="InductiveConstructor">clos</a> <a id="15156" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15156" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="15158" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15158" class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="15159" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="15161" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="15162" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15162" class="Bound">v</a><a id="15163" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="15165" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="15166" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15166" class="Bound">v&#39;</a><a id="15168" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="15170" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15170" class="Bound">ğ”¼v</a> <a id="15173" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15173" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a> <a id="15178" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15178" class="Bound">fv&#39;</a>
    <a id="15186" class="Keyword">with</a> <a id="15191" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15170" class="Bound">ğ”¼v</a> <a id="15194" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="15195" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4279" class="Function">AboveFun-âŠ‘</a> <a id="15206" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15178" class="Bound">fv&#39;</a> <a id="15210" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15173" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a><a id="15214" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="15216" class="Symbol">...</a> <a id="15220" class="Symbol">|</a> <a id="15222" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15224" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15224" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="15226" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15228" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15230" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15230" class="Bound">Mâ‡“c</a> <a id="15234" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15236" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15236" class="Bound">ğ•v</a> <a id="15239" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="15241" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="15243" class="Symbol">=</a>
      <a id="15251" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15253" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15224" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="15255" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15257" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="15259" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15230" class="Bound">Mâ‡“c</a> <a id="15263" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="15265" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#11026" class="Function">sub-ğ•</a> <a id="15271" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#15236" class="Bound">ğ•v</a> <a id="15274" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a> <a id="15279" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="15281" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

From `AboveFun v'` and `v' âŠ‘ v` we have `AboveFun v`.  Then with `ğ”¼ v c` we
obtain a closure `c` such that `Î³ âŠ¢ M â‡“ c` and `ğ• v c`. We conclude with an
application of `sub-ğ•` with `v' âŠ‘ v` to show `ğ• v' c`.


## Programs with function denotation terminate via call-by-name

The main lemma proves that if a term has a denotation that is above a
function, then it terminates via call-by-name. More formally, if
`Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` and `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'`, then `ğ”¼ v (clos M Î³')`. The proof is by
induction on the derivation of `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` we discuss each case below.

The following lemma, kth-x, is used in the case for the `var` rule.

    <a id="18190" class="Keyword">with</a> <a id="18195" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#16165" class="Function">â†“â†’ğ”¼</a> <a id="18199" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="18200" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18136" class="Bound">Î“</a><a id="18201" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="18203" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="18204" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18140" class="Bound">Î³</a><a id="18205" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="18207" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="18208" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18144" class="Bound">Î³&#39;</a><a id="18210" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="18212" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="18213" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18149" class="Bound">M</a><a id="18214" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="18216" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18157" class="Bound">ğ”¾Î³Î³&#39;</a> <a id="18221" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18174" class="Bound">d</a> <a id="18223" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18224" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#4279" class="Function">AboveFun-âŠ‘</a> <a id="18235" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18182" class="Bound">fv&#39;</a> <a id="18239" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18176" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a><a id="18243" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="18245" class="Symbol">...</a> <a id="18249" class="Symbol">|</a> <a id="18251" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="18253" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18253" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="18255" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="18257" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="18259" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18259" class="Bound">Mâ‡“c</a> <a id="18263" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="18265" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18265" class="Bound">ğ•v</a> <a id="18268" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="18270" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="18272" class="Symbol">=</a>
      <a id="18280" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="18282" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18253" class="Bound">c</a> <a id="18284" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="18286" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ¨</a> <a id="18288" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18259" class="Bound">Mâ‡“c</a> <a id="18292" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="18294" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#11026" class="Function">sub-ğ•</a> <a id="18300" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#18265" class="Bound">ğ•v</a> <a id="18303" class="Bound">v&#39;âŠ‘v</a> <a id="18308" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a> <a id="18310" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#139" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">âŸ©</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

* Case `var`. Looking up `x` in `Î³'` yields some closure, `clos M' Î´`,
  and from `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'` we have `ğ”¼ (Î³ x) (clos M' Î´)`. With the premise
  `AboveFun (Î³ x)`, we obtain a closure `c` such that `Î´ âŠ¢ M' â‡“ c`
  and `ğ• (Î³ x) c`. To conclude `Î³' âŠ¢ x â‡“ c` via `â‡“-var`, we 
  need `Î³' x â‰¡ clos M' Î´`, which is obvious, but it requires some
  Agda shananigans via the `kth-x` lemma to get our hands on it.

* Case `â†¦-elim`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ L Â· M â†“ v`.
  The induction hypothesis for `Î³ âŠ¢ L â†“ vâ‚ â†¦ v`
  gives us `Î³' âŠ¢ L â‡“ clos L' Î´` and `ğ• v (clos L' Î´)`.
  Of course, `L' â‰¡ Æ› N` for some `N`.
  By the induction hypothesis for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚`,
  we have `ğ”¼ vâ‚ (clos M Î³')`.
  Together with the premise `AboveFun v` and `ğ• v (clos L' Î´)`,
  we obtain a closure `c'` such that `Î´ âŠ¢ N â‡“ c'` and `ğ• v c'`.
  We conclude that `Î³' âŠ¢ L Â· M â‡“ c'` by rule `â‡“-app`.

* Case `â†¦-intro`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ Æ› N â†“ v â†¦ w`.
  We immediately have `Î³' âŠ¢ Æ› M â‡“ clos (Æ› M) Î³'` by rule `â‡“-lam`.
  But we also need to prove `ğ• (v â†¦ w) (clos (Æ› N) Î³')`.
  Let `c` by an arbitrary closure such that `ğ”¼ v c`.
  Suppose `v'` is greater than a function value.
  We need to show that `Î³' , c âŠ¢ N â‡“ c'` and `ğ• v' c'` for some `c'`.
  We prove this by the induction hypothesis for `Î³ , v âŠ¢ N â†“ v'`
  but we must first show that `ğ”¾ (Î³ , v) (Î³' , c)`. We prove
  that by the lemma `ğ”¾-ext`, using facts `ğ”¾ Î³ Î³'` and `ğ”¼ v c`.

* Case `âŠ¥-intro`. We have the premise `AboveFun âŠ¥`, but that's impossible.

* Case `âŠ”-intro`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)` and `AboveFun (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚)`
  and need to show `Î³' âŠ¢ M â†“ c` and `ğ• (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚) c` for some `c`.
  Again, by `AboveFun-âŠ”`, at least one of `vâ‚` or `vâ‚‚` is greater than
  a function.

  * Suppose both `vâ‚` and `vâ‚‚` are greater than a function value.
    By the induction hypotheses for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚` and `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚‚`
    we have `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ câ‚`, `ğ• vâ‚ câ‚`, `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ câ‚‚`, and `ğ• vâ‚‚ câ‚‚`
    for some `câ‚` and `câ‚‚`. Because `â‡“` is deterministic, we have `câ‚‚ â‰¡ câ‚`.
    Then by `ğ•âŠ”-intro` we conclude that `ğ• (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚) câ‚`.

  * Without loss of generality, suppose `vâ‚` is greater than a function
    value but `vâ‚‚` is not.  By the induction hypotheses for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ vâ‚`,
    and using `ğ•â†’WHNF`, we have `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚`
    and `ğ• vâ‚ (clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚)`.
    Then because `vâ‚‚` is not greater than a function, we also have
    `ğ• vâ‚‚ (clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚)`. We conclude that `ğ• (vâ‚ âŠ” vâ‚‚) (clos (Æ› N) Î³â‚)`.
    
* Case `sub`. We have `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v`, `v' âŠ‘ v`, and `AboveFun v'`.
  We need to show that `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ c` and `ğ• v' c` for some `c`.
  We have `AboveFun v` by `AboveFun-âŠ‘`,
  so the induction hypothesis for `Î³ âŠ¢ M â†“ v` gives us a closure `c`
  such that `Î³' âŠ¢ M â‡“ c` and `ğ• v c`. We conclude that `ğ• v' c` by `sub-ğ•`.


## Proof of denotational adequacy

The adequacy property is a corollary of the main lemma.
We have `âˆ… âŠ¢ Æ› N â†“ âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥`, so `â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)`
gives us `âˆ… âŠ¢ M â†“ âŠ¥ â†¦ âŠ¥`. Then the main lemma gives us
`âˆ… âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› Nâ€²) Î³` for some `Nâ€²` and `Î³`.

## Call-by-name is equivalent to beta reduction

As promised, we return to the question of whether call-by-name
evaluation is equivalent to beta reduction. In the chapter CallByName
we established the forward direction: that if call-by-name produces a
result, then the program beta reduces to a lambda abstraction.  We now
prove the backward direction of the if-and-only-if, leveraging our
results about the denotational semantics.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="reduceâ†’cbn"></a><a id="22133" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22133" class="Function">reduceâ†’cbn</a> <a id="22144" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22146" class="Symbol">âˆ€</a> <a id="22148" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="22149" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22149" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="22151" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22153" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3002" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="22155" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4150" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="22157" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2694" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="22158" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="22160" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="22161" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22161" class="Bound">N</a> <a id="22163" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="22165" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3002" class="InductiveConstructor">âˆ…</a> <a id="22167" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#3018" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="22169" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2694" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a> <a id="22171" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4150" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="22173" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#2694" class="InductiveConstructor">â˜…</a><a id="22174" class="Symbol">}</a>
           <a id="22187" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="22189" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22149" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="22191" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/LambdaReduction.md %}{% raw %}#894" class="Datatype Operator">â€”â† </a> <a id="22194" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4238" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›</a> <a id="22196" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22161" class="Bound">N</a>
           <a id="22209" class="Symbol">â†’</a> <a id="22211" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/v0.17/Data.Product.html#764" class="Function">Î£[</a> <a id="22214" href="{% endraw %}{{              <a id="22281" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2657" class="Function">âˆ…&#39;</a> <a id="22284" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#3020" class="Datatype Operator">âŠ¢</a> <a id="22286" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22149" class="Bound">M</a> <a id="22288" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#3020" class="Datatype Operator">â‡“</a> <a id="22290" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/CallByName.md %}{% raw %}#2477" class="InductiveConstructor">clos</a> <a id="22295" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="22296" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Untyped.md %}{% raw %}#4238" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">Æ›</a> <a id="22298" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22231" class="Bound">Nâ€²</a><a id="22300" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="22302" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22251" class="Bound">Î´</a>
<a id="22304" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22133" class="Function">reduceâ†’cbn</a> <a id="22315" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22315" class="Bound">Mâ€”â† Æ›N</a> <a id="22321" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="22323" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#21281" class="Function">adequacy</a> <a id="22332" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="22333" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Soundness.md %}{% raw %}#24729" class="Function">soundness</a> <a id="22343" href="{% endraw %}{{ site.baseurl }}{% link out/plfa/Adequacy.md %}{% raw %}#22315" class="Bound">Mâ€”â† Æ›N</a><a id="22348" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Suppose `M â€”â†  Æ› N`. Soundness of the denotational semantics gives us
`â„° M â‰ƒ â„° (Æ› N)`. Then by adequacy we conclude that
`âˆ…' âŠ¢ M â‡“ clos (Æ› Nâ€²) Î´` for some `Nâ€²` and `Î´`.

Putting the two directions of the if-and-only-if together, we
establish that call-by-name evaluation is equivalent to beta reduction
in the following sense.
